Commentary
This is a further reductio. The author shows that if the Mu'tazilite logic held, even the people of paradise would be in a cycle of gratitude and reward, making paradise a place of trial. But consensus (ijma') states paradise is not a place of obligation. Therefore, the Mu'tazilite position leads to absurdity and even to apostasy. The passage concludes with a strong condemnation.

Misconception: That reward is a necessary, contractual consequence of actions, leading to infinite regress in paradise.
Correction: Reward is by Allah's bounty and favor (faḍl) and paradise is not a place of obligation; thus no endless cycle occurs.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilite view collapses because it would turn paradise into a place of trial, contradicting the consensus that paradise is not a realm of obligation.

How would your daily motivation change if you truly internalized that paradise is not a paycheck but a gift of His grace? Would you still strive for good deeds? In what ways might your reliance on His mercy deepen?

Scriptural Proofs for the Punishment of the Grave
Al-Nasafi provides scriptural proofs for the punishment of the grave.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scriptural basis for the punishment of the grave, including key Quranic verses and hadith, and how these evidences are used in Sunni theology.

Core Idea
The punishment of the grave is proven by Qur'an, hadith, and the practice of the Muslim community.

This passage from al-Nasafi's Tabṣirat al-Adilla presents the evidence for the reality of the punishment of the grave, a key doctrine in Sunni Islam. Al-Nasafi begins by citing the consensus of the community and then provides a series of proofs from the Qur'an, the Prophet's teachings, and the ongoing supplication of Muslims. As you read, notice how each proof is presented and what kind of knowledge it yields.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation to grasp the flow of arguments.
The passage includes multiple proofs; note each one.
2
Identify the types of proof
List the different proofs al-Nasafi provides: two Quranic verses, the supplication of Muslims, and several hadiths. Notice how each is introduced.
3
Analyze the reasoning for each proof
For the Quranic verses, examine how al-Nasafi explains the implication (e.g., the immediate succession indicated by the letter 'fa' in the Noah verse). For the hadith, note the specific details about punishment for minor sins.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Al-Nasafi states that reports at the level of widespread transmission yield demonstrative knowledge. Consider why this is significant for theology.
This connects to the learning objective about scriptural evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أثبت جمهور الأمة عذاب القبر للكافرين ولبعض العصاة من المؤمنين والإنعام لأهل الطاعة في القبر وسؤال منكر ونكير لورود الدلائل السمعية في ذلك من نحو قوله تعالى: ﴿ النَّارُ يُعْرَضُونَ عَلَيْهَا غُدُوا وَعَشِيَّا وَيَوْمَ تَقُومُ السَّاعَةُ أَدْخِلُوا ءَالَ فِرْعَوْنَ أَشَدَّ الْعَذَابِ ﴾ فأثبت عرض آل فرعون على النار قبل القيامة غدوا وعشيا، وليس ذلك إلا عذاب القبر، وقال تعالى في شأن قوم نوح عليه السلام: ( مِّمَّا خَطِيئَيْهِمْ أَغْرِقُوا فَأَدْخِلُوا نَارًا ) والفاء للتعقيب والترتيب بلا تراخي، ولن يكون ذلك إلا في الدنيا إذ غرقهم كان فيها فيتعقب إدخال النار الإغراق، والمسلمون توارثوا الدعاء بقولهم : اللهم ربنا آتنا في الدنيا حسنة وفي الآخرة حسنة وقنا عذاب القبر النار، والأخبار الواردة في الباب الداخلة في حد الشهرة والاستفاضة وعذاب والخبر الذي بلغ هذا المبلغ يوجب العلم الاستدلالي منها قوله عليه السلام: استنزهوا من البول فإن عامة عذاب القبر منه وروى أنه مر بقبرين جديدين فقال: إنهما ليعذبان وما يعذبان بكبيرة أما أحدهما فإنه كان لا يستنزه من البول والآخر كان يمشي بالنميمة والخبر المعروف في الملكين اللذين يسألان الميت ومعهما مرزبتان وقول عمر له على إثري أو يكون معي عقلي؟ قال: بلى.
The majority of the community affirmed the punishment of the grave for disbelievers and for some disobedient believers, and blessings for the obedient in the grave, and the questioning by Munkar and Nakir, because of the transmitted evidences reaching that, such as the saying of God Most High: 'The Fire, they are exposed to it morning and evening, and on the Day the Hour arises, [it will be said], "Admit the family of Pharaoh into the severest punishment."' So He affirmed the exposure of the family of Pharaoh to the Fire before the Resurrection morning and evening, and that is nothing but the punishment of the grave. And God Most High said concerning the people of Noah (peace be upon him): 'Because of their sins they were drowned and made to enter a Fire.' The fa' indicates immediate succession and order without delay. And that can only be in this world, since their drowning was in it, so the entry into the Fire follows the drowning immediately. And the Muslims have inherited the supplication by their saying: 'O Allah, our Lord, give us in this world good and in the Hereafter good, and protect us from the punishment of the grave [and the Fire].' And the reports narrated on this topic that reach the level of general renown and widespread transmission, and the report that reaches this level yields demonstrative knowledge, among them his saying (peace be upon him): 'Cleanse yourselves from urine, for indeed the majority of the punishment of the grave is from it.' And it was narrated that he passed by two new graves and said: 'They are being punished, and they are not being punished for a major sin. As for one of them, he used not to cleanse himself from urine, and the other used to go about with malicious gossip.' And the well-known report about the two angels who question the deceased, and with them are two iron mallets, and the saying of Umar to him: 'Shall I be left with my mind?' He said: 'Yes.'
Source pages p. 1039

Commentary
This passage is a proof section establishing the reality of the punishment of the grave. Al-Nasafi begins by stating the consensus of the majority of the Muslim community (jumhur al-umma) on affirming the punishment of the grave for disbelievers and some disobedient believers, as well as blessings for the obedient, and the questioning by the angels Munkar and Nakir. He then provides scriptural evidences. First, he cites Qur'an 40:46, which mentions the exposure of Pharaoh's family to the Fire morning and evening before the Day of Resurrection, explaining that this can only refer to the punishment of the grave. Second, he cites Qur'an 71:25, concerning the people of Noah, where the letter 'fa' indicates immediate succession, meaning that after being drowned, they were entered into a Fire (i.e., the punishment of the grave) while still in this world. Third, he mentions the perpetual supplication of Muslims for protection from the punishment of the grave, indicating its recognition by the community. Fourth, he cites hadiths, such as the Prophet's command to clean oneself from urine because most of the punishment of the grave comes from it, and the hadith about two men being punished for minor sins, and the hadith about the two angels with iron mallets questioning the deceased, including the question of Umar about his intellect. The author concludes that such reports, reaching the level of wide transmission (al-shuhra wa al-istifada), yield demonstrative knowledge.

Key Terms
عذاب القبر (punishment of the grave)
سؤال منكر ونكير (questioning of Munkar and Nakir)
دلائل سمعية (scriptural evidences)
علم استدلالي (demonstrative knowledge)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the punishment of the grave is only for major sins.
Correction: Al-Nasafi cites a hadith where two people are punished for minor sins (not cleansing from urine and spreading gossip), showing that even minor sins can lead to punishment in the grave.

Checkpoint
Which Qur'anic verse does al-Nasafi use to prove that the punishment of the grave occurs before the Day of Resurrection?
A) The verse about Noah's people being drowned and entered into a Fire.
B) The verse about Pharaoh's family being exposed to the Fire morning and evening.
C) The verse about the believers being given good in this world and the Hereafter.
D) The verse about the questioning by Munkar and Nakir.

Key Takeaway
The punishment of the grave is an established doctrine supported by multiple scriptural evidences that, through their wide transmission, yield certain knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet said that the majority of the punishment of the grave is from not cleansing oneself from urine. When you last used the bathroom, were you fully mindful of purification? What is one concrete step you will take today to ensure you never neglect this again?
?
Umar asked the Prophet, 'Shall I be left with my mind?' He said, 'Yes.' Imagine the moment you are questioned by Munkar and Nakir. Do you truly believe that your current knowledge and practice will allow you to answer correctly? What one thing will you change this week to prepare for that moment?
?
The hadith mentions that a man was punished for spreading gossip (namima). Think of the last time you spoke about someone behind their back. How does that weigh on your soul? What will you do to purify your speech and seek forgiveness from Allah and the person you wronged?

Quranic Proofs for Punishment in the Grave
Al-Nasafi cites two Quranic verses and a supplication as proofs for punishment in the grave.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Nasafi uses Quranic verses and the Muslim supplication to establish punishment in the grave.

Core Idea
The Quran itself points to punishment before the Last Day — in the grave.

Al-Nasafi begins by stating the Sunni consensus on punishment in the grave, then immediately turns to the strongest proof: the Quran. The verses about Pharaoh and Noah implicitly show that punishment occurs before the Resurrection, which can only be the punishment of the grave. The inherited supplication further confirms this belief. In this lesson, we'll examine these three proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage with translation
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note how Al-Nasafi presents the majority position and then cites the first set of proofs.
2
Identify the three proofs
The passage lists three scriptural proofs: two from the Quran and one from the inherited supplication. Find each one and understand the reasoning behind each.
The first proof uses Quran 40:46, the second uses Quran 71:25 with the particle 'fa', and the third is the common supplication.
3
Understand the logical connection
For each proof, ask why it is considered evidence for punishment in the grave. For the verses, note the timing (before the Hour, immediate sequence). For the supplication, note its widespread acceptance.
The phrase 'ليس ذلك إلا عذاب القبر' explicitly identifies the punishment.

أثبت جمهور الأمة عذاب القبر للكافرين ولبعض العصاة من المؤمنين والإنعام لأهل الطاعة في القبر وسؤال منكر ونكير لورود الدلائل السمعية في ذلك من نحو قوله تعالى: ﴿ النَّارُ يُعْرَضُونَ عَلَيْهَا غُدُوا مستحيل والجواب عنه أن على أصل أبي الحسين الصالحي والكرامية يعذب ولا حياة له إذ ليست الحياة عندهم شرط لثبوت العلم على ما قررنا في أول مسألة وعند ابن الراوندي الحياة موجودة في كل ميت لأن الموت عنده ليس معنى مضاد للحياة بل هو آفة كلية معجزة عن الأفعال الاختيارية فلم تكن منافية للعلم. وهذه الأقاويل باطلة والصحيح أن الحياة شرط للعلم ولا تألم ولا تلذذ بدون العلم إلا أن الدلائل السمعية وردت بثبوت عذاب Chapter Five
1 - Discussion on Establishing the Punishment of the Grave:
The majority of the Ummah established the punishment of the grave for the disbelievers and for some of the sinful believers, and the bestowal of favor upon the obedient people in the grave, and the questioning by Munkar and Nakir, due to the arrival of scriptural evidences concerning that, such as His statement, the Exalted: 'The Fire, they are exposed to it morning and evening, and on the Day the Hour will be established, [it will be said], "Admit the family of Pharaoh into the severest punishment."' Thus He affirmed the exposure of the family of Pharaoh to the Fire before the Resurrection, morning and evening, and that is nothing other than the punishment of the grave. And He, the Exalted, said concerning the affair of the people of Noah, peace be upon him: 'Because of their sins they were drowned and then admitted into a Fire.' The 'fa' is for immediate sequence and order without delay, and that could only be in the world, since their drowning was in it, so the admission into the Fire follows the drowning. And the Muslims have inherited the supplication saying: 'O Allah, our Lord, give us in this world good and in the Hereafter good, and protect us from the punishment of the grave and the Fire.' And the reports narrated on this topic that have reached the level of well-knownness and wide transmission, and the report that has reached this level necessitates demonstrative knowledge. Among them is his statement, peace be upon him: 'Cleanse yourselves from urine, for indeed most of the punishment of the grave is from it.' And it is narrated that he passed by two new graves and said: 'They are both being punished, and they are not being punished for a great sin. As for one of them, he would not cleanse himself from urine, and the other used to go about with tale-bearing.' And the well-known report about the two angels who question the deceased, and with them are two iron maces, and the statement of 'Umar to him: 'Will my intellect be with me?' He said: 'Yes.' And the reports on this topic are many.
And the Jahmiyyah and some of the Mu'tazila denied that, because punishing one who has no life, and questioning him, and his answering is impossible. And the answer to it is that according to the principle of Abul-Husayn as-Salihi and the Karramiyya, he is punished while having no life, since life is not, according to them, a condition for the occurrence of knowledge, as we have established at the beginning of the issue. And according to Ibn ar-Rawandi, life exists in every dead person, because death in his view is not a meaning opposed to life, but rather a total impediment preventing voluntary actions, so it is not incompatible with knowledge. And these statements are invalid. And the correct view is that life is a condition for knowledge, and there is no pain nor pleasure without knowledge, except that the scriptural evidences have come affirming the punishment of the grave, so it is necessary to affirm its existence. Then it is among the possible things, since Allah, the Exalted, can restore to him a type of life to the extent that he experiences pain and pleasure, and thus He punishes him. And this is indicated by what we have narrated from the hadith of 'Umar, where he said: 'Will my intellect be with me?' And there is no existence of intellect without life. Likewise, it is indicated by His statement, the Exalted: 'Our Lord, You have caused us to die twice and You have given us life twice.' Then it is possible that He restores the spirit of life to him so that he lives, and it is possible that He establishes in him a type of life without restoring the spirit to him. And the refrain from affirmation (tawaqquf) on the part of our companions regarding the modality of the punishment of the grave, on this point, is whether life is established without restoring the spirit of life or with restoring the spirit of life. But they have no refrain regarding the fact that punishment without life cannot be conceived. That, rather, is the view of as-Salihi and the Karramiyya. And indeed
Source pages p. 1039

Commentary
This passage is a composite argument in which al-Nasafi defends the doctrine of punishment in the grave. He begins by stating the position of the majority of the Ummah: punishment for disbelievers and some sinful believers, reward for the obedient, and the questioning by Munkar and Nakir. These are established by scriptural proofs. He then cites several proofs: firstly, Quran 40:46, which shows that the family of Pharaoh are exposed to the fire 'morning and evening' before the Resurrection—this is interpreted as punishment in the grave. Secondly, Quran 71:25, where the people of Noah were drowned and then 'admitted into a fire'; the particle 'fa' indicates immediate sequence, so the fire must have occurred in this world after drowning, i.e., in the grave. Thirdly, the inherited supplication of Muslims asking for protection from the punishment of the grave. Fourthly, hadiths, including the command to cleanse from urine because much of the punishment of the grave comes from it, and the story of the two graves punished for minor sins. Fifthly, the well-known hadith of the two angels with maces who question the deceased, and the report that 'Umar asked if his intellect would remain with him, to which the Prophet replied affirmatively. After presenting these proofs, al-Nasafi reports the objection of the Jahmiyyah and some Mu'tazila: it is impossible to punish or question someone who has no life. He then presents two attempted answers that he rejects: first, the view of Abul-Husayn as-Salihi and the Karramiyya that life is not a condition for knowledge, so punishment without life is possible; second, the view of Ibn ar-Rawandi that death does not abolish life but only prevents voluntary actions, so life (and thus knowledge) persists. Al-Nasafi declares both views invalid. The correct position, he explains, is that life is indeed a condition for knowledge and sensation—but scriptural proofs necessitate affirming punishment in the grave. Therefore, it is possible for Allah to restore a type of life to the deceased, sufficient for them to experience pain or pleasure. This is supported by the hadith of 'Umar (which implies that intellect, and thus life, returns) and by Quran 40:11 about two deaths and two lives. He notes that it is possible that Allah restores the spirit of life, or grants a type of life without restoring the spirit. The companions of al-Nasafi (the Maturidis) suspend judgment on the modality—whether life is restored with or without the spirit—but they do not suspend judgment on the necessity of life for punishment; that necessity is agreed upon, unlike the view of as-Salihi and the Karramiyya.

Key Terms
عذاب القبر
منكر ونكير
الدلائل السمعية
غدو
عشي
فاء التعقيب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some interpret Quran 40:46 as referring only to the afterlife, not to an intermediate punishment.
Correction: Al-Nasafi argues that the mention of 'morning and evening' before the Hour indicates it occurs in the grave, not after Resurrection.

Checkpoint
Which verse does Al-Nasafi use to show that punishment occurs 'morning and evening' before the Resurrection?
A) Quran 71:25
B) Quran 40:46
C) Quran 2:201
D) Quran 3:185

Key Takeaway
The Quran explicitly mentions punishment before the Last Day, which can only be the punishment of the grave.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you knew that your state in the grave depends on your deeds now, what would you change about your daily habits? What specific action can you take today to prepare for the moment when Munkar and Nakir question you?
?
The Quran describes the people of Pharaoh being exposed to the fire morning and evening before the Hour. Does the thought of that punishment cause you to fear Allah in your private moments? How will you keep that awareness alive in your heart this week?
?
The supplication 'protect us from the punishment of the grave' has been transmitted from the earliest Muslims. When was the last time you sincerely made this dua for yourself and your loved ones? Will you commit to reciting it daily after every prayer?

Hadith Proofs for Punishment in the Grave
Al-Nasafi presents several hadiths as proofs for punishment in the grave, emphasizing their wide transmission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key hadiths Al-Nasafi uses to prove punishment in the grave and why he considers them authoritative.

Core Idea
The Prophet's own words and actions confirm the reality of punishment in the grave.

After citing Quranic proofs, Al-Nasafi turns to hadith reports that have reached the level of well-knownness and wide transmission. These reports provide demonstrative knowledge. In this lesson, we will examine three specific hadiths: the command to cleanse from urine, the incident of two graves, and the well-known report about the two angels and the questioning. Additionally, the hadith of 'Umar about his intellect is mentioned.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note that Al-Nasafi first states that these reports have reached a level that necessitates knowledge.
2
Identify each hadith
List the three main hadiths: (1) Urine cleansing, (2) Two graves, (3) Angels with maces. Also note the hadith of 'Umar.
The hadith about 'Umar asking about his intellect is included as proof that life returns.
3
Understand the evidentiary value
Al-Nasafi says these hadiths are 'within the bounds of well-knownness and wide transmission,' meaning they are mutawatir in meaning or mashhur. Ask why this is important for establishing belief.

الفصل الخامس
١ - الكلام في إثبات عذاب القبر :
أثبت جمهور الأمة عذاب القبر للكافرين ولبعض العصاة من المؤمنين والإنعام لأهل الطاعة في القبر وسؤال منكر ونكير لورود الدلائل السمعية في ذلك من نحو قوله تعالى: ﴿ النَّارُ يُعْرَضُونَ عَلَيْهَا غُدُوا وَعَشِيَّا وَيَوْمَ تَقُومُ السَّاعَةُ أَدْخِلُوا ءَالَ فِرْعَوْنَ أَشَدَّ الْعَذَابِ ﴾ فأثبت عرض آل فرعون على النار قبل القيامة غدوا وعشيا، وليس ذلك إلا عذاب القبر، وقال تعالى في شأن قوم نوح عليه السلام: ( مِّمَّا خَطِيئَيْهِمْ أَغْرِقُوا فَأَدْخِلُوا نَارًا ) والفاء للتعقيب والترتيب بلا تراخي، ولن يكون ذلك إلا في الدنيا إذ غرقهم كان فيها فيتعقب إدخال النار الإغراق، والمسلمون توارثوا الدعاء بقولهم : اللهم ربنا آتنا في الدنيا حسنة وفي الآخرة حسنة وقنا عذاب القبر النار، والأخبار الواردة في الباب الداخلة في حد الشهرة والاستفاضة والخبر الذي بلغ هذا المبلغ يوجب العلم الاستدلالي منها قوله عليه السلام: استنزهوا من البول فإن عامة عذاب القبر منه وروى أنه مر بقبرين جديدين فقال: "إنهما ليعذبان وما يعذبان بكبيرة أما أحدهما فإنه كان لا يستنزه من البول والآخر كان يمشي بالنميمة والخبر المعروف في الملكين اللذين يسألان الميت ومعهما مرزبتان وقول عمر له على إثري أو يكون معي عقلي؟ قال: بلى. والأخبار فى الباب كثيرة. وأنكرت الجهمية وبعض المعتزلة ذلك لما أن تعذيب من لا حياة له والسؤال منه والجواب منه مستحيل والجواب عنه أن على أصل أبي الحسين الصالحي والكرامية يعذب ولا حياة له إذ ليست الحياة عندهم شرط لثبوت العلم على ما قررنا في أول مسألة وعند ابن الراوندي الحياة موجودة في كل ميت لأن الموت عنده ليس معنى مضاد للحياة بل هو آفة كلية معجزة عن الأفعال الاختيارية فلم تكن منافية للعلم. وهذه الأقاويل باطلة والصحيح أن الحياة شرط للعلم ولا تألم ولا تلذذ بدون العلم إلا أن الدلائل السمعية وردت بثبوت عذاب القبر فلابد من القول بثبوته ثم هو من الممكنات إذ الله تعالى أن يعيد إليه نوع حياة مقدار ما يتألم ويتلذذ فيعذبه، ويدل عليه ما روينا من حديث عمر حيث قال: أو يكون معي عقلي؟ ولا وجود للعقل بدون الحياة، وكذا يدل عليه قوله تعالى: (رَبَّنَا أَمَتَنَا اثْنَيْنِ وَأَحْيِيتَنَا اثْنَتَيْنِ ثم من الجائز أن يعيد روح الحياة إليه فيحيى ومن الجائز أن يثبت فيه نوع حياة بدون إعادة الروح إليه، والتوقف لأصحابنا في كيفية عذاب القبر في هذا الحرف أن الحياة تثبت بدون إعادة روح الحياة أو مع إعادة روح الحياة فأما لا توقف لهم في أن لا يتصور التعذيب بدون الحياة إنما ذلك مذهب الصالحي والكرامية، وقد
Chapter Five
1 - Discussion on Establishing the Punishment of the Grave:
The majority of the Ummah established the punishment of the grave for the disbelievers and for some of the sinful believers, and the bestowal of favor upon the obedient people in the grave, and the questioning by Munkar and Nakir, due to the arrival of scriptural evidences concerning that, such as His statement, the Exalted: 'The Fire, they are exposed to it morning and evening, and on the Day the Hour will be established, [it will be said], "Admit the family of Pharaoh into the severest punishment."' Thus He affirmed the exposure of the family of Pharaoh to the Fire before the Resurrection, morning and evening, and that is nothing other than the punishment of the grave. And He, the Exalted, said concerning the affair of the people of Noah, peace be upon him: 'Because of their sins they were drowned and then admitted into a Fire.' The 'fa' is for immediate sequence and order without delay, and that could only be in the world, since their drowning was in it, so the admission into the Fire follows the drowning. And the Muslims have inherited the supplication saying: 'O Allah, our Lord, give us in this world good and in the Hereafter good, and protect us from the punishment of the grave and the Fire.' And the reports narrated on this topic that have reached the level of well-knownness and wide transmission, and the report that has reached this level necessitates demonstrative knowledge. Among them is his statement, peace be upon him: 'Cleanse yourselves from urine, for indeed most of the punishment of the grave is from it.' And it is narrated that he passed by two new graves and said: 'They are both being punished, and they are not being punished for a great sin. As for one of them, he would not cleanse himself from urine, and the other used to go about with tale-bearing.' And the well-known report about the two angels who question the deceased, and with them are two iron maces, and the statement of 'Umar to him: 'Will my intellect be with me?' He said: 'Yes.' And the reports on this topic are many.
And the Jahmiyyah and some of the Mu'tazila denied that, because punishing one who has no life, and questioning him, and his answering is impossible. And the answer to it is that according to the principle of Abul-Husayn as-Salihi and the Karramiyya, he is punished while having no life, since life is not, according to them, a condition for the occurrence of knowledge, as we have established at the beginning of the issue. And according to Ibn ar-Rawandi, life exists in every dead person, because death in his view is not a meaning opposed to life, but rather a total impediment preventing voluntary actions, so it is not incompatible with knowledge. And these statements are invalid. And the correct view is that life is a condition for knowledge, and there is no pain nor pleasure without knowledge, except that the scriptural evidences have come affirming the punishment of the grave, so it is necessary to affirm its existence. Then it is among the possible things, since Allah, the Exalted, can restore to him a type of life to the extent that he experiences pain and pleasure, and thus He punishes him. And this is indicated by what we have narrated from the hadith of 'Umar, where he said: 'Will my intellect be with me?' And there is no existence of intellect without life. Likewise, it is indicated by His statement, the Exalted: 'Our Lord, You have caused us to die twice and You have given us life twice.' Then it is possible that He restores the spirit of life to him so that he lives, and it is possible that He establishes in him a type of life without restoring the spirit to him. And the refrain from affirmation (tawaqquf) on the part of our companions regarding the modality of the punishment of the grave, on this point, is whether life is established without restoring the spirit of life or with restoring the spirit of life. But they have no refrain regarding the fact that punishment without life cannot be conceived. That, rather, is the view of as-Salihi and the Karramiyya. And indeed
Source pages p. 1039

Commentary
This passage is a composite argument in which al-Nasafi defends the doctrine of punishment in the grave. He begins by stating the position of the majority of the Ummah: punishment for disbelievers and some sinful believers, reward for the obedient, and the questioning by Munkar and Nakir. These are established by scriptural proofs. He then cites several proofs: firstly, Quran 40:46, which shows that the family of Pharaoh are exposed to the fire 'morning and evening' before the Resurrection—this is interpreted as punishment in the grave. Secondly, Quran 71:25, where the people of Noah were drowned and then 'admitted into a fire'; the particle 'fa' indicates immediate sequence, so the fire must have occurred in this world after drowning, i.e., in the grave. Thirdly, the inherited supplication of Muslims asking for protection from the punishment of the grave. Fourthly, hadiths, including the command to cleanse from urine because much of the punishment of the grave comes from it, and the story of the two graves punished for minor sins. Fifthly, the well-known hadith of the two angels with maces who question the deceased, and the report that 'Umar asked if his intellect would remain with him, to which the Prophet replied affirmatively. After presenting these proofs, al-Nasafi reports the objection of the Jahmiyyah and some Mu'tazila: it is impossible to punish or question someone who has no life. He then presents two attempted answers that he rejects: first, the view of Abul-Husayn as-Salihi and the Karramiyya that life is not a condition for knowledge, so punishment without life is possible; second, the view of Ibn ar-Rawandi that death does not abolish life but only prevents voluntary actions, so life (and thus knowledge) persists. Al-Nasafi declares both views invalid. The correct position, he explains, is that life is indeed a condition for knowledge and sensation—but scriptural proofs necessitate affirming punishment in the grave. Therefore, it is possible for Allah to restore a type of life to the deceased, sufficient for them to experience pain or pleasure. This is supported by the hadith of 'Umar (which implies that intellect, and thus life, returns) and by Quran 40:11 about two deaths and two lives. He notes that it is possible that Allah restores the spirit of life, or grants a type of life without restoring the spirit. The companions of al-Nasafi (the Maturidis) suspend judgment on the modality—whether life is restored with or without the spirit—but they do not suspend judgment on the necessity of life for punishment; that necessity is agreed upon, unlike the view of as-Salihi and the Karramiyya.

العقل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some argue that these hadiths are isolated and not sufficient for establishing doctrinal beliefs.
Correction: Al-Nasafi counters that these reports have reached the level of well-knownness and wide transmission, making them authoritative for demonstrative knowledge.

Checkpoint
Which hadith mentions the two angels with iron maces?
A) The hadith about urine cleansing
B) The hadith about two graves
C) The well-known report about Munkar and Nakir
D) The hadith of 'Umar about intellect

Key Takeaway
Numerous well-known hadiths from the Prophet explicitly describe punishment in the grave, making it an established belief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that the Prophet explicitly warned that 'most of the punishment of the grave is from urine.' When you use the restroom, do you take care to avoid drops of urine? Does this hadith change how you will go about your daily hygiene from this moment on?
?
The Prophet pointed to two graves: one punished for not cleansing from urine, the other for spreading gossip (ناميمة). Is there a person you have spoken about behind their back recently? Will you repent and seek to mend that relationship today before you meet the angels with iron maces?
?
Umar asked the Prophet, 'Will my intellect be with me?' and the Prophet said 'Yes.' Your intellect that you use now to plan, reason, and doubt will be with you in the grave. In that moment, looking back at your life, what will your intellect tell you? Will it accuse you of negligence or confirm your sincerity?

8 min
Refuting the Objection to Punishment in the Grave
Al-Nasafi refutes the Jahmiyyah's objection and presents the correct Sunni response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Jahmiyyah's objection to punishment in the grave and Al-Nasafi's correct response based on scriptural evidence and divine power.

Core Idea
Punishment in the grave is possible because Allah can restore life to the deceased.

Having presented the scriptural proofs, Al-Nasafi now addresses the main objection: that it is impossible to punish someone without life. He rejects two flawed answers from other groups and gives the correct Sunni response: life is necessary for sensation, but Allah can restore a type of life to the deceased. He then discusses the Maturidi position of suspending judgment on the modality while affirming the necessity of life for punishment.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
Read the passage with translation. Pay attention to the objection from the Jahmiyyah and Mu'tazila, then the two rejected answers, and finally the correct view.
2
Understand the rejected views
Al-Nasafi mentions two incorrect responses: as-Salihi and the Karramiyya say life is not needed for knowledge; Ibn ar-Rawandi says death does not remove life. Why does Al-Nasafi reject them?
3
Grasp the correct argument
The correct view is that life is a condition for pain/pleasure, but since scripture affirms punishment, Allah can create a temporary life. Note the proof from the hadith of 'Umar and Quran 40:11.
4
Learn about tawaqquf
Al-Nasafi explains that the Maturidis suspend judgment on whether the restored life is the spirit or another type, but they do not suspend on the necessity of life for punishment.

Commentary
This passage is a composite argument in which al-Nasafi defends the doctrine of punishment in the grave. He begins by stating the position of the majority of the Ummah: punishment for disbelievers and some sinful believers, reward for the obedient, and the questioning by Munkar and Nakir. Thirdly, the inherited supplication of Muslims asking for protection from the punishment of the grave. Fourthly, hadiths, including the command to cleanse from urine because much of the punishment of the grave comes from it, and the story of the two graves punished for minor sins. Fifthly, the well-known hadith of the two angels with maces who question the deceased, and the report that 'Umar asked if his intellect would remain with him, to which the Prophet replied affirmatively. He notes that it is possible that Allah restores the spirit of life, or grants a type of life without restoring the spirit. Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Punishment in the grave is impossible because the dead are completely insentient and cannot be punished.
Correction: Al-Nasafi argues that Allah can restore a type of life to the deceased, making them capable of experiencing pain and pleasure.

Checkpoint
According to Al-Nasafi, why is punishment in the grave possible despite the dead having no life?
A) Life is not needed for punishment.
B) Allah can restore a type of life to the deceased.
C) The dead are still alive in a different sense.
D) Punishment is only spiritual.

Key Takeaway
While punishment in the grave requires life, Allah can restore a type of life to the deceased, making it possible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that every moment after your death you will be held accountable and feel the reality of your deeds? Or do you live as if death is an end and the grave is just soil? What in your life today reflects your belief in the grave's questioning?
?
You have heard that Allah can restore a type of life to the deceased. Does this certainty change your attitude towards your own future state? Are you preparing for that moment, or is it a distant thought you push aside?
?
If you were to face the grave tonight, what would you wish you had done differently? How does this lesson compel you to change one action today that will make that moment lighter?

The Reality of Punishment in the Grave
Defines the correct view on punishment of the grave and refutes deniers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi position on punishment in the grave, including its necessity despite the requirement of life, and the refutation of deniers.

Core Idea
Punishment in the grave requires life, but Allah can restore life in a way unknown to us.

The reality of punishment in the grave is a contested issue. Some groups deny it because a dead body lacks life and sensation. In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi refutes these deniers and establishes the correct view: that life is a condition, but Allah can grant life specifically for punishment. He also clarifies the Maturidi position on the modality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opposing views
Read the passage and note the groups that deny punishment in the grave and their reasoning.
The deniers are the Jahmiyya and some Mu'tazila.
2
Understand the refutations
Imam al-Nasafi presents and then refutes the counterviews of al-Salihi, the Karramiyya, and Ibn al-Rawandi.
These views attempt to justify punishment without life or claim life persists.
3
Learn the correct Maturidi view
The correct view is that life is necessary for punishment, but scriptural proofs compel its affirmation.
Allah can restore a kind of life sufficient for pain or pleasure.
4
Examine the evidence
The hadith of Umar and the Quranic verse about two deaths and lives are cited as proofs.
The hadith implies intellect persists, which requires life.
5
Note the suspension on modality
Maturidi scholars suspend judgment on whether the spirit returns or a special life is given.
They agree that life is required but remain silent on how it is restored.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأنكرت الجهمية وبعض المعتزلة ذلك لما أن تعذيب من لا حياة له والسؤال منه والجواب منه مستحيل والجواب عنه أن على أصل أبي الحسين الصالحي والكرامية يعذب ولا حياة له إذ ليست الحياة عندهم شرط لثبوت العلم على ما قررنا في أول مسألة وعند ابن الراوندي الحياة موجودة في كل ميت لأن الموت عنده ليس معنى مضاد للحياة بل هو آفة كلية معجزة عن الأفعال الاختيارية فلم تكن منافية للعلم. وهذه الأقاويل باطلة والصحيح أن الحياة شرط للعلم ولا تألم ولا تلذذ بدون العلم إلا أن الدلائل السمعية وردت بثبوت عذاب القبر فلابد من القول بثبوته ثم هو من الممكنات إذ الله تعالى أن يعيد إليه نوع حياة مقدار ما يتألم ويتلذذ فيعذبه، ويدل عليه ما روينا من حديث عمر الله حيث قال: أو يكون معي عقلي؟ ولا وجود للعقل بدون الحياة، وكذا يدل عليه قوله تعالى: (رَبَّنَا أَمَتَنَا اثْنَيْنِ وَأَحْيِيتَنَا اثْنَتَيْنِ) ثم من الجائز أن يعيد روح الحياة إليه فيحيى ومن الجائز أن يثبت فيه نوع حياة بدون إعادة الروح إليه، والتوقف لأصحابنا في كيفية عذاب القبر في هذا الحرف أن الحياة تثبت بدون إعادة روح الحياة أو مع إعادة روح الحياة فأما لا توقف لهم في أن لا يتصور التعذيب بدون الحياة إنما ذلك مذهب الصالحي والكرامية، وقد نص على اشتراط الحياة عندنا الشيخ أبو الحسن الرستغفني وشيخنا أبو منصور - رحمهما الله نص أيضا على اشتراط ذلك، ونص على أن التوقف في إعادة الروح وعدم إعادتها.
The Jahmiyya and some Mu'tazila denied that, because torturing one who has no life, questioning him, and answering from him are impossible. The answer is that according to the principle of Abu al-Husayn al-Salihi and the Karramiyya, he is tortured without life, since life is not a condition for the establishment of knowledge according to them, as we established in the first issue. And according to Ibn al-Rawandi, life exists in every dead person because death in his view is not a meaning opposite to life, but rather a total incapacity, hindering voluntary actions, so it is not incompatible with knowledge. These sayings are false. The correct view is that life is a condition for knowledge, and there is no pain or pleasure without knowledge, except that the scriptural proofs have come establishing the punishment of the grave, so it is necessary to affirm it. Then it is among possibilities, since Allah the Exalted can restore a kind of life to him to the extent that he feels pain and pleasure, and thus punish him. This is supported by what we narrated from the hadith of Umar where he said: 'Will my intellect be with me?' And there is no existence of intellect without life. Similarly, it is supported by His statement: 'Our Lord, You have caused us to die twice and given us life twice.' Then it is possible that He returns the spirit of life to him so that he lives, and it is possible that He establishes a kind of life in him without returning the spirit. The suspension of judgment among our companions regarding the modality of punishment of the grave in this matter is whether life is established without the return of the spirit of life or with the return of the spirit of life. As for them, they have no suspension in that punishment cannot be conceived without life – that is only the school of al-Salihi and the Karramiyya. And the condition of life with us has been explicitly stated by Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Rustughfani and our Shaykh Abu Mansur – may Allah have mercy on them – they also explicitly stated that condition, and they explicitly stated that the suspension is regarding the return of the spirit or its non-return.
Source pages p. 1040

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of those who deny punishment of the grave and an exposition of the correct Maturidi position. The author begins by stating that the Jahmiyya and some Mu'tazila denied punishment of the grave because torturing someone without life is impossible, as are questioning and answering. The initial response is to note that according to Abu al-Husayn al-Salihi and the Karramiyya, punishment without life is possible because life is not a condition for knowledge (which is necessary for sensation). Similarly, Ibn al-Rawandi holds that life exists in every dead person since death is merely an incapacity, not the absence of life. The author then declares these views false. The correct view is that life is a condition for knowledge, and there is no pain or pleasure without knowledge. However, scriptural proofs (sam'iyyat) have established the punishment of the grave, so it must be affirmed. It is possible because Allah can restore a kind of life to the deceased sufficient for pain and pleasure. The author supports this with the hadith of Umar asking if his intellect will be with him, and the Qur'anic verse about being given life twice. He then explains that it is possible for Allah to either return the spirit (ruh) or grant a kind of life without it. The Maturidi scholars suspend judgment on the modality (kayfiyya) of punishment, i.e., whether life is restored with or without the spirit, but they have no doubt that punishment requires life; that view belongs only to al-Salihi and the Karramiyya. Finally, he names two authorities—Abu al-Hasan al-Rustughfani and Abu Mansur al-Maturidi—who explicitly state that life is a condition and that the suspension concerns the return of the spirit.

Key Terms
عذاب القبر
الحياة
إعادة الروح
الجهمية
المعتزلة
الكرامية
أبو الحسين الصالحي
ابن الراوندي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Punishment in the grave is impossible because the dead have no life.
Correction: The correct view is that life is necessary for punishment, but Allah can restore a kind of life to the deceased for punishment, as attested by scripture.

Checkpoint
According to the correct Maturidi view, what is required for punishment in the grave?
A) Only the body without life
B) Life, but the modality of how life is restored is not specified
C) The return of the spirit only
D) Knowledge without life

Key Takeaway
The Maturidi position affirms punishment in the grave because Allah can restore life, even though the modality of that life is unknown.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson confirms that after death, you will not simply cease to exist—you will be made to feel. How does the certainty of being held to account immediately after burial change what you fear most about death? Are you prepared to face that moment tonight?
?
The Maturidis suspend judgment on the modality of life in the grave, yet they affirm its reality without hesitation. Is your faith in the unseen (الغيب) strong enough to accept this truth without demanding to know 'how'? Where in your life do you secretly demand proof before believing?
?
Umar (رضي الله عنه) asked about his intellect in the grave—not his wealth or family. When you imagine your own grave, what occupies your thoughts: your worldly achievements or the state of your intellect and faith? What does that reveal about your priorities right now?

Life as a Condition and Tawaqquf on the Soul's Return
Narrates the Maturidi position on life as a condition and tawaqquf on soul's return.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maturidi position that life is a condition for certain attributes, and their stance of tawaqquf regarding the return of the soul after death.

Core Idea
Life is a condition; the soul's return is left open.

In this passage, two foundational Maturidi scholars—Abu al-Hasan al-Rustughfani and Abu Mansur al-Maturidi—affirm that life is a necessary condition (shart) for certain divine acts or human attributes. They also adopt a position of tawaqquf (suspension of judgment) on whether the soul returns to the body after death. This sets the stage for later discussions on the state of the deceased and the rejection of Mu'tazili views.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then its translation. Note the key terms: حياة (life), توقف (suspension), إعادة الروح (return of the soul).
2
Identify the two claims
There are two claims: one affirming life as a condition, the other stating tawaqquf on the soul's return. Notice how the passage presents them as positions of the named scholars.
3
Consider the significance
Think about why these positions matter: they clarify Maturidi epistemology regarding the state of the dead and the conditions for knowledge or sensation.
4
Connect to the broader discussion
This passage introduces a view that will be contrasted with Mu'tazili denial of life in the dead. The tawaqquf shows caution where revelation is silent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نص على اشتراط الحياة عندنا الشيخ أبو الحسن الرستغفني وشيخنا أبو منصور - رحمهما الله - نص أيضا على اشتراط ذلك، ونص على أن التوقف في إعادة الروح وعدم إعادتها.
Our scholar Abu al-Hasan al-Rustughfani and our master Abu Mansur - may Allah have mercy on them - stated the condition of life according to us, and he also stated the condition of that, and he stated that there is a pause (tawaqquf) regarding the return of the soul and its non-return.
Source pages p. 1041

Commentary
This passage reports the doctrinal position of two key Maturidi scholars: Abu al-Hasan al-Rustughfani and Abu Mansur al-Maturidi. They affirm that life (al-hayat) is a condition (shart) for something, likely for knowledge or sensation, as the context shows. Additionally, they state a stance of tawaqquf (suspension of judgment) concerning the return of the soul (i'adat al-ruh) after death and its non-return. This tawaqquf means they neither definitively affirm nor deny whether the soul returns to the body in the barzakh; they leave the matter open. This sets the stage for the following discussion refuting the Mu'tazila who deny life in the dead.

Key Terms
الحياة (al-hayat)
التوقف (al-tawaqquf)
إعادة الروح (i'adat al-ruh)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did Abu al-Hasan al-Rustughfani and Abu Mansur state about life?
A) Life is not necessary
B) Life is a condition (shart)
C) Life is impossible after death
D) Life is only for the living

Key Takeaway
The Maturidi scholars affirmed life as a condition and adopted a stance of tawaqquf on the soul's return, leaving the matter open.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The scholars suspended judgment on the soul's return because the evidence was inconclusive. Are you willing to admit when you lack certainty about a matter of faith, or do you force answers where they are not given? How can you practice intellectual humility today?
?
If life is a condition for perception, and the dead can perceive, then your most private actions are witnessed even after death. What is one habit you engage in only when you think no one is watching, and how does this knowledge change your resolve?
?
The Maturidis did not deny the soul's return; they simply left it open. Is there a belief you have held too rigidly without evidence, perhaps out of fear or tradition? Will you examine that belief in light of the sources, or continue to hold it dogmatically?

5 min
Turning the Mu'tazila's Distinction Against Them
Argues that structure is a condition for being alive.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author argues that the condition of structure applies to being alive, not just being receptive to life, thereby cornering the Mu'tazila.

Core Idea
The condition for being alive cannot be escaped.

The author continues his refutation by addressing a potential escape route for the Mu'tazila. They had distinguished structure as a condition for receptivity to life, not for life itself. The author flips this: it is a condition for being alive, and they have no way out.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the original text carefully. Notice the phrase 'قيل لهم: ربما تنفصلون' which signals a response to a potential objection.
The author anticipates the Mu'tazila might try to separate themselves from a previous argument.
2
Identify the distinction
The Mu'tazila claim that structure is a condition for being receptive to life, not for being alive. Understand the difference.
They are trying to limit the scope of the condition.
3
See the turn
The author counters: 'شرط لكونه حيًا لا لكونه قابلاً للحياة' – it is a condition for being alive, not for being receptive to life. This turns their own distinction against them.
The author asserts that the condition applies to the very existence of life.
4
Recognize the result
The author concludes that they have no escape from this argument. Reflect on why this is a strong refutation.
The Mu'tazila cannot deny that structure is needed for life itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قيل لهم: ربما تنفصلون ممن يقول هي شرط لهما جميعًا أو قلب عليكم فقال: شرط لكونه حيًا لا لكونه قابلاً للحياة ولا انفصال لهم عنه، والله الموفق. ولا يقال لو كانت في الميت حياة لعاينها، لأنا نقول: الحياة لا تشاهد في الشاهد بل تعرف بظهور أثرها، وهو الأفعال الاختيارية إذ لا فعل بدون القدرة ولا قدرة بدون الحياة فتعرف ثبوت الحياة بثبوت الفعل الاختياري بواسطة ثبوت القدرة، ثم القدرة وإن كانت لا يتصور وجودها بدون الحياة فوجود الحياة يتصور بدون القدرة فيقيم الله تعالى بالميت حياة ولا يخلق له قدرة فلا يوجد منه فعل اختياري فلا يعرف وجود الحياة، هذا كما أن من أصابته سكتة لا يعرف وجود الحياة فيه لما أنه لا قدرة له فلا يتصور منه الفعل فلا تعرف حياته، والله الموفق.
It was said to them: Perhaps you will separate yourselves from those who say it is a condition for both, or the argument may be turned against you, and he said: It is a condition for being alive, not for being receptive to life, and they have no escape from that. And Allah is the grantor of success. And it cannot be said that if there were life in the dead, it would be perceived, for we say: Life is not perceived in the phenomenal world (al-shahid) but is known by the appearance of its effect, which is voluntary actions (al-af'al al-ikhtiyariyyah), for there is no action without power (qudrah) and no power without life. Thus the existence of life is known by the existence of voluntary action through the intermediary of the existence of power. Then, although power cannot be conceived without life, the existence of life can be conceived without power. So Allah Almighty may place life in the dead without creating power for him, so no voluntary action occurs from him, and thus the existence of life is not known. This is like one who is struck by a seizure (saktah): his life is not known because he has no power, so no action can be conceived from him, so his life is not known. And Allah is the grantor of success.
Source pages p. 1042

Commentary
This passage provides two additional refutations. First, the author turns the Mu'tazila's own distinction against them. If they say structure is only a condition for receptivity to life, one can counter by saying it is a condition for being alive itself, and the Mu'tazila have no way to separate themselves from this view. Second, the author preempts an objection: 'If there were life in the dead, it would be perceived.' He answers that life in this world (al-shahid) is not directly seen but is inferred from its effects, specifically voluntary actions (al-af'al al-ikhtiyariyyah). Voluntary actions require power (qudrah), and power requires life. However, life can exist without power. God can grant life to the dead without granting power, so no voluntary action occurs, and life remains unknown to observers. He illustrates this with the analogy of a person in a coma (saktah): such a person is alive but has no power to act, so his life is not apparent. Thus, the absence of observable effects does not disprove life.

Key Terms
الحياة (al-hayat)
الشرط (al-shart)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, the condition of structure applies to which of the following?
A) Being receptive to life
B) Being alive
C) Both life and receptivity
D) Neither life nor receptivity

Key Takeaway
The author turns the Mu'tazila's own distinction against them by asserting that the condition applies to being alive, leaving them no escape.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What 'escape routes' have you constructed to avoid facing a condition that is actually necessary for your spiritual life? Will you drop them now?
?
The Mu'tazila tried to separate the condition from life itself. Where in your own life have you tried to separate a necessary practice from its spiritual reality, thinking you could have the benefit without the commitment?
?
The author ends with 'والله الموفق' — success comes from Allah alone. In what specific area of your life do you need to stop relying on your own reasoning and humbly submit to Allah's condition?

Answering the Objection about Perceiving Life
Responds to the objection that life would be perceived if present.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why life is not directly perceivable but is known through its effects, particularly voluntary actions.

Core Idea
Life is known by its effects, not by direct observation.

The author now addresses a common objection: if there were life in the dead, it would be observable. He explains that life in this world is not seen directly; it is inferred from voluntary actions, which require power (qudrah) and power requires life. However, life can exist without power, as in the case of a coma.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and response
Read the Arabic passage starting from 'ولا يقال لو كانت في الميت حياة لعاينها' to the end. Note the objection and the author's response.
The objection is hypothetical: 'if there were life, it would be perceived'.
2
Understand the inference
The author states that life is known by the appearance of its effect: voluntary actions. Actions require power, and power requires life. Trace this chain: life → power → action.
This is a causal inference.
3
Note the exception
The author explains that life can exist without power. God can grant life without granting power, so no voluntary action occurs, and life remains unknown.
This addresses the objection directly.
4
Examine the analogy
The author compares this to a person in a seizure (saktah). In such a state, the person is alive but has no power to act, so life is not apparent.
The analogy makes the concept concrete.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قيل لهم: ربما تنفصلون ممن يقول هي شرط لهما جميعًا أو قلب عليكم فقال: شرط لكونه حيًا لا لكونه قابلاً للحياة ولا انفصال لهم عنه، والله الموفق. ولا يقال لو كانت في الميت حياة لعاينها، لأنا نقول: الحياة لا تشاهد في الشاهد بل تعرف بظهور أثرها، وهو الأفعال الاختيارية إذ لا فعل بدون القدرة ولا قدرة بدون الحياة فتعرف ثبوت الحياة بثبوت الفعل الاختياري بواسطة ثبوت القدرة، ثم القدرة وإن كانت لا يتصور وجودها بدون الحياة فوجود الحياة يتصور بدون القدرة فيقيم الله تعالى بالميت حياة ولا يخلق له قدرة فلا يوجد منه فعل اختياري فلا يعرف وجود الحياة، هذا كما أن من أصابته سكتة لا يعرف وجود الحياة فيه لما أنه لا قدرة له فلا يتصور منه الفعل فلا تعرف حياته، والله الموفق.
It was said to them: Perhaps you will separate yourselves from those who say it is a condition for both, or the argument may be turned against you, and he said: It is a condition for being alive, not for being receptive to life, and they have no escape from that. And Allah is the grantor of success. And it cannot be said that if there were life in the dead, it would be perceived, for we say: Life is not perceived in the phenomenal world (al-shahid) but is known by the appearance of its effect, which is voluntary actions (al-af'al al-ikhtiyariyyah), for there is no action without power (qudrah) and no power without life. Thus the existence of life is known by the existence of voluntary action through the intermediary of the existence of power. So Allah Almighty may place life in the dead without creating power for him, so no voluntary action occurs from him, and thus the existence of life is not known. This is like one who is struck by a seizure (saktah): his life is not known because he has no power, so no action can be conceived from him, so his life is not known. And Allah is the grantor of success.

Commentary
This passage provides two additional refutations. First, the author turns the Mu'tazila's own distinction against them. If they say structure is only a condition for receptivity to life, one can counter by saying it is a condition for being alive itself, and the Mu'tazila have no way to separate themselves from this view. Second, the author preempts an objection: 'If there were life in the dead, it would be perceived.' Voluntary actions require power (qudrah), and power requires life. However, life can exist without power. Key Terms
الحياة (al-hayat)
القدرة (al-qudrah)
الفعل الاختياري (al-fi'l al-ikhtiyari)
السكتة (al-saktah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Life, if present, would always be directly observable.
Correction: Life is known by its effects (voluntary actions), not by direct perception. It can exist without observable effects if power is absent.

Checkpoint
How is life known in the phenomenal world according to the author?
A) By direct sensory perception
B) By revelation
C) By the appearance of voluntary actions
D) By the presence of bodily structure

Key Takeaway
Life is not directly perceived but inferred from voluntary actions; life can exist without power, so lack of observable action does not disprove life.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You believe the dead are alive in their graves, but you cannot perceive it. Do your daily choices — the way you speak of the dead, your fear of their fate, your prayers for them — reflect that belief, or do you live as if death is the end? What is one concrete action you will take this week to remind yourself that the life of the grave is real?
?
The saktah analogy describes a person alive but powerless. When you feel spiritually numb or unable to do good, do you still trust that your soul is alive? How does the truth that God can give life without power give you hope when you are in a 'seizure' of weakness?
?
This argument proves that absence of evidence (no visible action) is not evidence of absence (no life). What unseen realities of your faith — like Allah’s love, the angels, or your own sincerity — have you doubted because you cannot 'see' them? Will you commit today to knowing them by their effects rather than demanding direct proof?

Quranic Proof of Life After Death for Sensation
Proof citation with two Quranic verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Maturidi school uses Quranic verses to prove that the dead are granted life to experience pleasure or pain.

Core Idea
Quranic verses prove that martyrs are alive, supporting life after death for sensation.

After establishing the theological necessity of sensation in the barzakh, the author turns to scriptural proof. He cites two clear Quranic verses that affirm the life of martyrs, which he uses as evidence that Allah can grant life to the dead for the purpose of pleasure or pain. This passage grounds the Maturidi position in revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then read the translation. Notice the direct citation of Quranic verses.
2
Identify the two verses
Locate Surah Al Imran (3:169-170) and Surah Al-Baqarah (2:154). Note how both affirm that martyrs are alive and experiencing reward.
The author uses these as evidence for a general principle.
3
Reflect on the doctrinal implication
Consider how these verses support the Maturidi claim that the dead can be granted life for sensation, countering those who limit such life to martyrs only.
This is a scriptural proof for the barzakh life.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأدلة على أن الميت يعطي حياة ليحس الإلذاذ أو العذاب: والدليل على قيام الحياة بمن أراد الله تعالى إلذاذه أو إيلامه قوله تعالى: وَلَا تَحْسَبَنَّ الَّذِينَ قُتِلُوا فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ أَمْوَاتًا بَلْ أَحْيَاءٌ عِندَ رَبِّهِمْ يُرْزَقُونَ فَرِحِينَ. وقوله: وَلَا تَقُولُوا لِمَن يُقْتَلُ فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ أَمْوَاتٌ بَلْ أَحْيَاءٌ وَلَكِن لَا تَشْعُرُونَ. والله الموفق.
The proofs that the dead are given life to feel pleasure or pain: The evidence for the subsistence of life in those for whom Allah Almighty wills pleasure or pain is His saying: 'Do not think those who are killed in the way of Allah are dead; rather, they are alive with their Lord, provided for, rejoicing.' And His saying: 'And do not say of those who are killed in the way of Allah that they are dead; rather, they are alive, but you do not perceive.' And Allah is the grantor of success.
Source pages p. 1042

Commentary
This passage provides scriptural evidence for the Maturidi position that the dead (specifically martyrs) are granted a form of life in the barzakh to experience pleasure or pain. Two Quranic verses are cited. The first is Surah Al Imran (3:169-170): 'Do not think those killed in the way of Allah are dead; rather, they are alive with their Lord, provided for, rejoicing.' The second is Surah Al-Baqarah (2:154): 'And do not say of those who are killed in the way of Allah that they are dead; rather, they are alive, but you do not perceive.' These verses explicitly affirm that martyrs are alive and experiencing reward, countering the Mu'tazila and others who deny any form of life after death before the Resurrection. The author uses them to support the argument that life can be given to the dead for the purpose of sensation (al-ildhadh or al-alam).

Key Terms
الحياة (al-hayat)
الإلذاذ (al-ildhadh)
العذاب (al-'adhab)
الشهداء (al-shuhada')

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quranic verses about martyrs being alive apply only to martyrs and cannot be used as general proof for life after death for all dead.
Correction: The author uses these verses as evidence for the general principle that Allah can grant life to the dead for sensation, not limited to martyrs.

Checkpoint
What is the primary proof given for the claim that the dead are given life for sensation?
A) Rational argument
B) Consensus of scholars
C) Quranic verses
D) Prophetic hadith

Key Takeaway
The Quran explicitly states that martyrs are alive, providing scriptural basis for the belief that the dead can experience sensation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read these verses, do you truly internalize that those who die in Allah's way are alive and rejoicing in His presence? How does this reality change the way you view your own efforts and sacrifices for His sake? Are you willing to give up comfort for a life that is real and everlasting?
?
If you knew that the martyrs are witnesses to your daily actions, would you live differently? Is your faith so deep that you would be ready to trade this fleeting world for that promised life of sensation and joy?
?
The Quran says 'you do not perceive' their life. Does your lack of perception cause you to doubt, or does it strengthen your reliance on Allah's words? What would it cost you to live today as if the unseen martyrs are watching and your own barzakh life depends on your choices?

Life in the Dead: Rational Proof and Quranic Evidence
Al-Nasafi refutes the Mu'tazilite claim about life in the dead and provides Quranic proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Nasafi's rational argument that life can exist without observable signs and his Quranic proof that martyrs are alive after death.

Core Idea
Life can be hidden; its presence is inferred through necessary conditions, not direct observation.

This passage from al-Nasafi tackles a key theological debate: can the dead have life? He first refutes the Mu'tazilite condition for life, then establishes a rational chain linking life, power, and voluntary action. Finally, he confirms his argument with Quranic verses about martyrs, who are described as alive and receiving sustenance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Mu'tazilite claim
Read the opening sentence where al-Nasafi states the Mu'tazilite position: bodily structure is a condition for being capable of life, not for life itself.
The Mu'tazilites argued that a dead body cannot have life because it lacks the structure to support it.
2
Follow the counterargument
Notice how al-Nasafi presents a dialectical response: someone could say structure is a condition for both life and capability, or reverse the claim, leaving the Mu'tazilites with no escape.
This is a common kalam technique of 'qīla lahum' (it was said to them).
3
Understand the rational proof
Work through the chain: voluntary actions require power, power requires life. Life is known by its effects (voluntary actions). But life can exist without power, so a dead person may have life without observable actions.
Al-Nasafi uses the analogy of a person struck by apoplexy to illustrate hidden life.
4
Examine the Quranic evidence
Read the two Quranic verses provided (3:168-169 and 2:154) which explicitly state that martyrs are not dead but alive, even if humans do not perceive it.
These verses directly support al-Nasafi's argument that life can be imperceptible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
زعمت المعتزلة أن البنية ليست بشرط لكونه حيا بل هي شرط لكونه قابلاً للحياة. قيل لهم: ربما تنفصلون ممن يقول هي شرط لهما جميعًا أو قلب عليكم فقال: شرط لكونه حيًا لا لكونه قابلاً للحياة ولا انفصال لهم عنه، والله الموفق. ولا يقال لو كانت في الميت حياة لعاينها، لأنا نقول: الحياة لا تشاهد في الشاهد بل تعرف بظهور أثرها، وهو الأفعال الاختيارية إذ لا فعل بدون القدرة ولا قدرة بدون الحياة فتعرف ثبوت الحياة بثبوت الفعل الاختياري بواسطة ثبوت القدرة، ثم القدرة وإن كانت لا يتصور وجودها بدون الحياة فوجود الحياة يتصور بدون القدرة فيقيم الله تعالى بالميت حياة ولا يخلق له قدرة فلا يوجد منه فعل اختياري فلا يعرف وجود الحياة، هذا كما أن من أصابته سكتة لا يعرف وجود الحياة فيه لما أنه لا قدرة له فلا يتصور منه الفعل فلا تعرف حياته، والله الموفق. الأدلة على أن الميت يعطي حياة ليحس الإلذاذ أو العذاب: والدليل على قيام الحياة بمن أراد الله تعالى الذاذه أو إيلامه قوله تعالى: {وَلَا تَحْسَبَنَّ الَّذِينَ قُتِلُوا فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ أَمْوَاتًا بَلْ أَحْيَاء عِندَ رَبِّهِمْ يُرْزَقُونَ فَرِحِينَ}. وقوله {وَلَا تَقُولُوا لِمَن يُقْتَلُ في سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ أَمْوَاتٌ بَلْ أَحْيَاء وَلَكِن لَا تَشْعُرُونَ} والله الموفق.
The Mu'tazila claimed that the bodily structure is not a condition for being alive, but rather it is a condition for being capable of life. It was said to them: Perhaps you will separate yourselves from someone who says it is a condition for both, or he turns [the argument] upon you and says: it is a condition for being alive, not for being capable of life, and there is no separation for them from it, and God is the Grantor of success. And it is not said: if there were life in the dead, we would observe it, for we say: life is not witnessed in the witnessed [world] but is known by the appearance of its effect, which is voluntary actions, for there is no action without power and no power without life, so the existence of life is known by the existence of voluntary action through the intermediary of the existence of power. Then, even though power cannot be conceived to exist without life, the existence of life can be conceived without power. So God Almighty establishes life in the dead and does not create power for him, so no voluntary action occurs from him, and thus the existence of life is not known. This is like one who is struck by apoplexy: the existence of life in him is not known because he has no power, so no action can be conceived from him, so his life is not known. And God is the Grantor of success. The evidences that the dead are given life to feel pleasure or pain: The proof for the existence of life in one whom God wills to give pleasure or pain is His statement: {And do not think those who are killed in the way of God are dead; rather, they are alive with their Lord, receiving provision, rejoicing.} And His statement: {And do not say of those who are killed in the way of God, 'They are dead'; rather, they are alive, but you perceive not.} And God is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 1042

Commentary
This passage is a two-part argument: first, a rational refutation of the Mu'tazilite position that bodily structure is only a condition for capability of life, not for being alive; second, a scriptural proof that martyrs are alive. Al-Nasafi begins by stating the Mu'tazilite claim: the bodily structure (al-bunya) is not a condition for being alive in itself, but rather a condition for being capable of receiving life. The author then presents a counterargument: one might say that the structure is a condition for both being alive and being capable, or they could reverse the argument and claim it is a condition for being alive, not for capability, leaving them with no way out. Next, he addresses an expected objection: if there were life in a dead person, we would directly observe it. He refutes this by explaining that life in this world is not directly observable; it is only known through its effects, specifically voluntary actions. The chain of reasoning is: voluntary actions require power, and power requires life. Therefore, if we see voluntary action, we infer power, and from power we infer life. However, the reverse is not always true: life can exist without power. God can place life in a dead person but withhold power, so no voluntary action occurs, and thus the presence of life remains hidden. He illustrates this with a person struck by apoplexy (sakta) who has life but lacks power, so no one can perceive his life. This establishes that life can exist without manifest signs. Finally, he provides the scriptural proof from the Quran: verses 3:168-169 and 2:154, which explicitly state that those killed in God's way are not dead but alive, receiving sustenance and rejoicing. This confirms that God gives life to the dead for reward or punishment.

Key Terms
الحياة
القدرة
الفعل الاختياري
الميت
الشاهد
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if life is present, it must be directly observable.
Correction: Al-Nasafi explains that life is known by its effects (voluntary actions), not by direct sight. Life can exist without observable effects, as with martyrs or a person in a coma.

Checkpoint
According to al-Nasafi, how is life in a dead person known if it cannot be observed?
A) By direct observation
B) By the presence of voluntary actions
C) By the presence of power
D) It cannot be known at all

Key Takeaway
Life can be present without observable signs, as with martyrs, and the Quran and rational reasoning confirm this.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you measure your own spiritual aliveness by visible actions alone, or do you trust that God sees life where no one else can? What would it mean for you to act with faith in the unseen vitality that God can grant even when your deeds feel barren?
?
The martyrs are described as 'alive with their Lord, receiving provision, rejoicing' while you cannot perceive it. Does this truth change how you view death and sacrifice? Will you live today as if the unseen life after death is more real than the one you breathe?
?
Al-Nasafi argues that life is known by its effect—voluntary action. If your life had no voluntary acts of obedience today, would there be any evidence that your soul is alive in faith? What one action can you commit to right now that would prove your spiritual life is real?
